<script type="application/ld+json">{"@context":"https:\/\/schema.org","@type":"BlogPosting","headline":"The Emerging Dynamics of Deepfake Scam Campaigns on the Web","name":"The Emerging Dynamics of Deepfake Scam Campaigns on the Web","description":"A technical analysis of deepfake technology uncovers how cybercriminals utilize AI-generated videos of public figures to execute sophisticated scams.","url":"https:\/\/unit42.paloaltonetworks.com\/dynamics-of-deepfake-scams\/","mainEntityOfPage":"https:\/\/unit42.paloaltonetworks.com\/dynamics-of-deepfake-scams\/","datePublished":"August 29, 2024","articleBody":"Executive Summary\r\nOur researchers discovered dozens of scam campaigns using deepfake videos featuring the likeness of various public figures, including CEOs, news anchors and top government officials. These campaigns appear in English, Spanish, French, Italian, Turkish, Czech and Russian. Each campaign typically targets potential victims in a single country, including Canada, Mexico, France, Italy, Turkey, Czechia, Singapore, Kazakhstan and Uzbekistan.\r\n\r\nDue to their infrastructural and tactical similarities, we believe that many of these campaigns likely stem from a single threat actor group. We have observed this threat actor group using deepfake videos to spread fake investment schemes and fake government-sponsored giveaways.\r\n\r\nAs of June 2024, we had discovered hundreds of domains being used to promote these campaigns. Each domain has been accessed an average of 114,000 times globally since going live, based on our passive DNS (pDNS) telemetry.\r\n\r\nStarting with a campaign promoting an investment scheme called Quantum AI, we studied the infrastructure behind this campaign to track its spread over time. Through this infrastructure investigation, we discovered several additional deepfake campaigns leveraging completely different themes that the same threat actor group created and promoted. These additional scam campaigns used different languages and the likeness of different public figures, suggesting that each campaign is intended for a different target audience.\r\n\r\nDespite the use of generative AI (GenAI) in these campaigns, traditional investigative techniques remain useful to identify the hosting infrastructure leveraged by these threat actors. As the malicious usage of deepfake technology increases among threat actors, so should defenders\u2019 efforts to proactively detect and prevent these types of attacks.\r\n\r\nCustomers of Palo Alto Networks are better protected from these attacks via Advanced URL Filtering, which will continue to detect and block websites that are used to propagate deepfake-based scam campaigns.\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nRelated Unit 42 Topics\r\nScams, Phishing\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nDiscovering Quantum AI Hosting Infrastructure\r\nTo study the Quantum AI campaign, we decided to analyze the infrastructure behind the websites hosting these attacks. Starting with an initial seed set of detections from our deepfake video detection pipeline, we then looked for additional websites serving up known malicious videos. We observed several Quantum AI-related videos that adversaries were widely sharing via websites hosted on newly registered domains.\r\n\r\nUpon further investigation, we identified that the videos themselves were primarily hosted on a single domain:\r\n\r\n \tBelmar-marketing[.]online\r\n\r\nNext, we searched for other web pages that served video files from this domain and also contained keywords like Quantum AI in the HTML content.\r\n\r\nThrough this process, we were able to uncover dozens of other scam pages using these videos as a lure. We then used the content on these web pages as well as the pathnames of the video files to create signatures to expand our detections. (See the Indicators of Compromise section for example URLs.)\r\n\r\nIn May 2024, we noticed that an increasing number of Quantum AI videos were being hosted on other domains as well, including the following:\r\n\r\n \tAi-usmcollective[.]click\r\n \tFortunatenews[.]com\r\n \tFiirststreeeet[.]top\r\n\r\nWe also discovered some sites built using website builders that were promoting the same Quantum AI scam. In these cases, the attackers re-hosted the video directly on the site via the website builder, not on one of the shared video-hosting domains mentioned above.\r\nQuantum AI Example Videos and Web Pages\r\nIn Figures 1-7, we present examples of Quantum AI scam web pages and videos discovered by our video analysis pipeline and infrastructure-based investigation. In most of these examples, the scam web page was hosted on a newly registered domain, and the video was hosted as an .mp4 file on one of the shared video-hosting domains mentioned above (e.g., belmar-marketing[.]online).\r\n\r\nIn most cases, the attackers appear to have started with a legitimate video and added on their own AI-generated audio. Finally, they used lip-syncing technology to modify the lip movement of the speaker to match the AI-generated audio. Most of the videos use Elon Musk as their celebrity of choice, although we discovered a handful of examples using other public figures as well:\r\n\r\n \tTucker Carlson\r\n \tLee Hsien Loong, the former Prime Minister of Singapore\r\n \tTharman Shanmugaratnam, the President of Singapore (as of June 2024)\r\n\r\n[caption id=\"attachment_136454\" align=\"alignnone\" width=\"1327\"] Figure 1. Huerwlleiss-herton[.]pro, a website using an Elon Musk deepfake video to promote the Quantum AI scam.[\/caption][caption id=\"attachment_136456\" align=\"alignnone\" width=\"1179\"] Figure 2. Bitquantumai[.]com, a website using a deepfake video of Elon Musk and Tucker Carlson to promote the Quantum AI scam.[\/caption][caption id=\"attachment_136458\" align=\"alignnone\" width=\"1190\"] Figure 3. Quantumal[.]xyz, a website used to promote the Quantum AI scam. The web page asks for a referral code to log in.[\/caption]\r\n\r\n[caption id=\"attachment_136460\" align=\"alignnone\" width=\"1260\"] Figure 4. Screenshot of an Elon Musk deepfake video used to promote the Quantum AI scam. In the video, deepfake-Elon claims that Quantum AI is the \u201cworld\u2019s first quantum computing software developed by his team with a success rate of 91%.\u201d[\/caption]\r\n\r\n[caption id=\"attachment_136504\" align=\"alignnone\" width=\"786\"] Figure 5. Another screenshot of a different Elon Musk deepfake video used to promote the Quantum AI scam.[\/caption]\r\n\r\n[caption id=\"attachment_136462\" align=\"alignnone\" width=\"1238\"] Figure 6. Griffinware-tm.cloud, a website using a deepfake video of Lee Hsien Loong, the former Prime Minister of Singapore, to promote the Quantum AI scam.[\/caption]\r\n\r\n[caption id=\"attachment_136464\" align=\"alignnone\" width=\"1354\"] Figure 7. A screenshot of a deepfake video of Tharman Shanmugaratnam, the current President of Singapore, used to promote the Quantum AI scam.[\/caption]\r\nDeepfake Campaign Discovery and Tracking\r\nAfter investigating the Quantum AI scam campaign, we explored broader trends surrounding these deepfake campaigns as a whole.\r\nUncovering Additional Deepfake Scams\r\nIn addition to the Quantum AI scam, we also investigated the other videos that were present on these video-hosting domains. In doing so, we were able to uncover several other scam campaigns (likely propagated by the same threat actor group), many of which use deepfake videos as a lure. These deepfake videos typically use the likeness of public figures like CEOs, news anchors or top government officials.\r\n\r\nWe discovered deepfake videos in several different languages, including English, Spanish, French, Italian, Turkish, Czech and Russian. Each campaign typically targets potential victims in a single country, including Canada, Mexico, France, Italy, Turkey, Czechia, Singapore, Kazakhstan and Uzbekistan.\r\n\r\nSimilar to the Quantum AI scam campaign, these videos add AI-generated audio on top of an existing video and use lip-syncing tools to alter the lip movement of the speaker to match the new audio. Visitors to these web pages are prompted to register with their name and phone number, and they are instructed to await a call from an account manager or representative.\r\n\r\nIn many of these cases, we discovered several newly registered domains hosting the same content (and the same deepfake video lure). This means that each of these scam web pages is part of a larger campaign, not just a one-off scam web page.\r\n\r\nFor example, in the case of the KazMunayGas scam shown below in Figure 8, we found scammers using the same video across several recently registered domains, including:\r\n\r\n \tAigroundwork[.]top\r\n \tAitfinside[.]shop\r\n \tBlock4aischeme[.]top\r\n \tSystemaigroundwork[.]shop\r\n\r\nThe Indicators of Compromise section provides a more complete list of these domains.\r\n\r\n[caption id=\"attachment_136466\" align=\"alignnone\" width=\"1169\"] Figure 8. Coinframework[.]top, a scam website using an AI-manipulated video of a Kazakh news anchor to promote a fake giveaway started by KazMunayGas, the state-owned oil and gas company of Kazakhstan.[\/caption][caption id=\"attachment_136468\" align=\"alignnone\" width=\"1181\"] Figure 9. Riseanalyze[.]click, a website linked to from coinframework[.]top. This website contains a registration form for the KazMunayGas-themed scam.[\/caption]Although the languages and impersonation-targets of these scam campaigns are different, they share the following similarities:\r\n\r\n \tThey all use similar deepfake techniques\r\n \tThey have similar calls to action\r\n \tThey host their videos on a small, shared set of domains (that do not seem to be used for any other purpose than to host these scam videos)\r\n\r\nThis suggests that these campaigns can most likely be attributed to a single threat actor group.\r\n\r\nWe present some selected examples of these additional scam campaigns in Figures 10-15.\r\n\r\n[caption id=\"attachment_136470\" align=\"alignnone\" width=\"1228\"] Figure 10. Invest-toolavenue[.]shop, a scam website using an AI-manipulated video of Patrick Pouyann\u00e9 (TotalEnergies CEO) to promote a fake giveaway supposedly created by TotalEnergies, a French multinational energy and petroleum company.[\/caption][caption id=\"attachment_136472\" align=\"alignnone\" width=\"1163\"] Figure 11. Invest-toolavenue[.]shop, continued from Figure 10.[\/caption]\r\n\r\n[caption id=\"attachment_136502\" align=\"alignnone\" width=\"900\"] Figure 12. Capitalflow-skillful.shop, a scam website using an AI-manipulated video of Andr\u00e9s Manuel L\u00f3pez, the President of Mexico, to promote a fake \u201cMexican Investment Society Project.\u201d[\/caption]\r\n\r\n[caption id=\"attachment_136474\" align=\"alignnone\" width=\"1228\"] Figure 13. Untamedal.top, a scam website using an AI-manipulated video of Giorgia Meloni, the Prime Minister of Italy, to promote a fake state-sponsored investment program called FinInvest.[\/caption]\r\n\r\n[caption id=\"attachment_136476\" align=\"alignnone\" width=\"1172\"] Figure 14. Hugeproject[.]shop, a World Bank-themed scam website using an AI-manipulated video of a woman claiming to represent an international investment bank.[\/caption][caption id=\"attachment_136478\" align=\"alignnone\" width=\"1170\"] Figure 15. Hugeproject[.]shop, continued from Figure 14.[\/caption]\r\nCampaign Activity Over Time\r\nWhile these campaigns started about a year ago, we observed a large spike of newly observed domains (shown in Figure 16) in February 2024. Unlike typical phishing or malware domains, these domains are relatively long-lived, with an average active time of 142 days.\r\n\r\n[caption id=\"attachment_136480\" align=\"alignnone\" width=\"712\"] Figure 16. The number of newly observed domains hosting deepfake videos over time.[\/caption]\r\n\r\nFigure 17 shows that the number of active domains exponentially increased until about March 2024, and the total number of active domains has remained steady to the present day.\r\n\r\n[caption id=\"attachment_136482\" align=\"alignnone\" width=\"712\"] Figure 17. The number of active domains hosting deepfake videos over time.[\/caption]\r\n\r\nFurthermore, it is concerning to note that these domains have a high reach, with each domain being accessed an average of 114,000 times since they first went live, based on pDNS telemetry. The actual number is likely much higher.\r\nHosting Infrastructure Analysis\r\nGoing with the current trend of camouflaging in shared hosting infrastructure, 86.7% of these campaign domains are using the same popular content delivery network (CDN). Multiple IP addresses from the CDN host the same content across different geographic locations, with the U.S., the Netherlands and Russia being the top 3 locations. The utilization of CDNs makes it difficult to attribute the campaign to a particular threat actor or geolocation.\r\n\r\nWe observed that the attackers primarily hosted their videos on a small set of attacker-owned domains. Attackers presumably did this to circumvent takedown issues that could occur on more popular video-hosting platforms.\r\n\r\nUntil April 2024, we observed that the deepfake videos were predominantly hosted on belmar-marketing[.]online. However, starting in May 2024, the attackers began to rotate their video hosting locations more frequently. As such, we observed that videos were now mainly hosted on fiirststreeeet[.]top, ai-usmcollective[.]click and fortunatenews[.]com.\r\n\r\nLooking for web pages that link to videos hosted on these domains has been very valuable for tracking the spread of these campaigns so far. We will continue to monitor for new video-hosting domains as these campaigns progress.\r\nHow the Quantum AI Scam Works\r\nDuring our research, we observed posts and ads promoting Quantum AI on various social media platforms (shown in Figures 18-20). According to the Australian National Anti-Scam Center, scammers often first use these sorts of social media ads or fake news articles to link to scam web pages that ask for the victim user\u2019s contact information.\r\n\r\n[caption id=\"attachment_136484\" align=\"alignnone\" width=\"580\"] Figure 18. Social media post linking to a Quantum AI scam web page.[\/caption]\r\n\r\n[caption id=\"attachment_136486\" align=\"alignnone\" width=\"487\"] Figure 19. Messaging platform post linking to a Quantum AI scam web page.[\/caption]\r\n\r\n[caption id=\"attachment_136488\" align=\"alignnone\" width=\"1920\"] Figure 20. Social media post using a video to promote the Quantum AI scam.[\/caption]\r\n\r\nAfter visiting the scam landing page and filling out a form to sign up for the platform, one of the scammers gives the victim a phone call. In this call, the scammer tells the victim they\u2019ll need to pay around $250 to access the platform.\r\n\r\nThe scammer instructs the victim to download a special app so that they can \u201cinvest\u201d more of their funds. Within the app, a dashboard appears to show small profits. From there, the scammers continue persuading the victim to deposit more of their money and may even allow the victim to withdraw a small amount of money as a way to gain trust.\r\n\r\nFinally, when the victim tries to withdraw their funds, the scammers either demand withdrawal fees, or cite some other reason (e.g., tax issues) for not being able to get their funds back. The scammers may then lock the victim out of their account and pocket the remaining funds, causing the victim to have lost the majority of the money that they put into the \u201cplatform.\u201d\r\nOverview of the Web-Based Deepfake Scam Landscape\r\nQuantum AI is not the only scam that adversaries are using involving deepfakes. In this section we\u2019ll discuss other techniques and services that they have been using.\r\n\r\nIn early 2024, a company lost $25 million to attackers who used deepfake technology to impersonate their chief financial officer on a video conferencing call. While video conferencing deepfakes have received significant attention as a result of this attack, web-based deepfake scams are an emerging threat that researchers should monitor as well.\r\n\r\n2024 is predicted to be the largest voting year in history. Over 60 countries are holding significant elections this year, meaning that around half the world's population could be directly affected by these events. In response, researchers have raised concerns about the potential for deepfakes to promote political misinformation. However, the impact of deepfakes is not limited to the political domain. Cybercriminals have already been creating and sharing deepfake videos for their own malicious purposes.\r\nDeepfakes Used to Promote Scams and Phishing Attacks\r\nSince the advent of GenAI, attackers have used deepfakes to promote political misinformation, and even to further voter outreach. For example, in early 2024, a Democratic political consultant used an audio deepfake of Joe Biden to discourage voters in the state of New Hampshire from voting in the upcoming primary election.\r\n\r\nIn India, politicians actively encouraged their supporters to create deepfakes to promote their own candidacies. In 2022, an unknown threat actor used manipulated deepfake videos of Ukrainian President Volodymir Zelensky as a part of information warfare in the Russia-Ukraine war.\r\n\r\nNow, we are seeing cybercriminals start to use deepfake media to promote their own scams and phishing attacks as well. In recent months, reporters have observed scams impersonating figures like Elon Musk (shown in Figure 21), Bill Gates and Warren Buffett to peddle fake cryptocurrencies, giveaways and other investment schemes. These are created with the ultimate goal of stealing funds from victims. (Our previous tweets on this topic have more details.)\r\n\r\n[caption id=\"attachment_136490\" align=\"alignnone\" width=\"918\"] Figure 21. Screenshot of an Elon Musk deepfake video seen on patriotsmaga2024[.]com, a website promoting the sale of fake \u201cTrump Liberty Coins.\u201d[\/caption]Previously, these attackers might have used paid actors to promote their scams (e.g., by creating videos purporting to be a client who profited from a fake investment scheme). With the increasing popularity and effectiveness of tools that use AI to generate content (e.g., images, audio and video), attackers are now able to create these videos in a cheaper and more convincing way.\r\nDeepfakes as a Service\r\nOur researchers have encountered cybercriminals selling, discussing and trading deepfake tooling and creation services across forums, social media chat channels and instant messaging platforms. These tools and services offer capabilities for generating deceptive and malicious content including audio, video and imagery. The ecosystem surrounding deepfake creation and tooling is alive and vibrant, and cybercriminals are selling a variety of options from face swapping tools to deepfake videos.\r\n\r\nFace swapping tools like Swapface (shown in Figure 22) range in price from free to over $249 a month. Adversaries abuse these tools, placing the videos they create on diverse platforms and social media platforms. Swapface offers user-friendly filters and face swapping that operates in real time, allowing users to alter or replace faces in videos.\r\n\r\n[caption id=\"attachment_136492\" align=\"alignnone\" width=\"786\"] Figure 22. Swapface tooling subscription cost.[\/caption]\r\n\r\nThe criminal application of deepfake tooling and creation services and tools includes the following activities:\r\n\r\n \tFacilitating the creation of fake identities\r\n \tCommitting bank fraud\r\n \tOrchestrating disinformation campaigns\r\n \tBypassing know-your-customer verification checks\r\n \tPerforming cryptocurrency theft\r\n\r\nThese services can manipulate visuals and audio with alarming precision, leading to significant ethical and security concerns. The cost of generating a deepfake video can vary widely, typically ranging from $60 to $500, reflecting the complexity and quality of the requested forgery.\r\n\r\nAs seen in Figure 23, we also discovered messaging platform channels specifically advertising the creation of deepfake videos for scam purposes.\r\n\r\n[caption id=\"attachment_136494\" align=\"alignnone\" width=\"1297\"] Figure 23. Messaging platform channel dedicated to deepfake generation services.[\/caption]\r\n\r\nThe accessibility and range of costs make deepfakes particularly versatile tools for maliciousness, posing challenges for both individuals and institutions trying to safeguard against fraud and misinformation.\r\nConclusion\r\nDespite the use of GenAI in these campaigns, traditional investigative techniques remain useful to identify the hosting infrastructure leveraged by these threat actors. As threat actors increase their use of deepfake technology, organizations should also proactively defend against these types of attacks.\r\n\r\nPalo Alto Networks researchers will continue to monitor these deepfake-based scam campaigns and continue to discover and investigate additional deepfake-based scam campaigns. As such, we can ensure that our customers are better protected from them via Advanced URL Filtering.\r\nIndicators of Compromise\r\nDeepfake Scam Examples\r\n[caption id=\"attachment_136916\" align=\"alignnone\" width=\"783\"] Figure 24.     function addStyle(parent, id, def) {
        if (!parent) {
        return;
        }
        var style = doc.createElement('style');
        style.id = id;
        style.innerHTML = def;
        parent.appendChild(style);

            return;
        }

	function getCookie(cname) {
	 	var name = cname + "=";
  		var decodedCookie = decodeURIComponent(document.cookie);
		var ca = decodedCookie.split(';');
  		for(var i = 0; i <ca.length; i++) {
    			var c = ca[i];
    			while (c.charAt(0) == ' ') {
     				 c = c.substring(1);
    			}
    			if (c.indexOf(name) == 0) {
    				 return c.substring(name.length, c.length);
    			}
  		}
  		return "";
	}

function callMainSitePrismaNavHTML(){
    
    var referrer_domain = 'https://www.paloaltonetworks.com';
    sessionStorage.setItem("domain",referrer_domain);
    if(referer == 'Prisma'){
        var menu_url = referrer_domain+'/_jcr_content/globals/cleanHeaderPrisma.prismaRenderer.html';
        searchResultsPagePath = referrer_domain+"/search/prismasearch";
        }
    if(referer == 'Cortex'){
        var menu_url = referrer_domain+'/_jcr_content/globals/cleanHeaderCortex.cortexRenderer.html';	
        searchResultsPagePath = referrer_domain+"/search/cortexsearch";	
    }
    if(referer == 'Sase'){
        var menu_url = referrer_domain+'/_jcr_content/globals/cleanHeaderSase.saseRenderer.html';
        searchResultsPagePath = referrer_domain+"/search/sasesearch";
    }
    if(referer == 'Unit'){
        var menu_url = 'https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/themes/unit42-v6/unit-nav-renderer.php';
        searchResultsPagePath = referrer_domain+"/content/pan/en_US/search/unit42search";
		    }
    if(referer == 'Ngfw'){
        var menu_url = 'https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/themes/unit42-v6/ngfw-cdss-nav-renderer.php';
        searchResultsPagePath = referrer_domain+"/search/ngfwcdsssearch";
    }
    httpGet(menu_url,'menu_html');
    document.getElementById('main-nav-menu-cont').removeAttribute("style");
}
function addStyle(styles) {            
    /* Create style document */
    var css = document.createElement('style');
    css.type = 'text/css';

    if (css.styleSheet) 
        css.styleSheet.cssText = styles;
    else 
        css.appendChild(document.createTextNode(styles));

    /* Append style to the tag name */
    document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(css);
}
function httpGet(theUrl,req_type) {
    if (window.XMLHttpRequest) { // code for IE7+, Firefox, Chrome, Opera, Safari
        xmlhttp=new XMLHttpRequest();
    } else {// code for IE6, IE5
        xmlhttp=new ActiveXObject("Microsoft.XMLHTTP");
    }
    xmlhttp.onreadystatechange=function()
    {
        if (xmlhttp.readyState==4 && xmlhttp.status==200)
        {
            if(req_type == 'menu_html'){
            var nav_text = xmlhttp.responseText.replaceAll('https://static.cloud.coveo.com/searchui/v2.9159/js/CoveoJsSearch.Lazy.min.js', '');
            nav_text = nav_text.replaceAll('src="/', 'src="'+maindomain_lang+'/');
            nav_text = nav_text.replaceAll("'/content", "'"+maindomain_lang+"/content");
                        
            document.getElementById("PAN_2021_NAV_ASYNC").innerHTML = nav_text.replaceAll('href="/', 'href="'+maindomain_lang+'/');

            var lozad_back = document.getElementsByClassName('lozad-background');
            Array.prototype.forEach.call(lozad_back, function(el) {
            // Do stuff here
            var el_back_img_path = el.getAttribute('data-background-image');
            var first_pos = el_back_img_path.indexOf("'");
            var last_pos = el_back_img_path.indexOf("'",first_pos+1);
            el_back_img_path = el_back_img_path.substring(first_pos+1,last_pos);
            el.setAttribute("data-background-image",main_site_url+el_back_img_path);
            });
            }
            if(req_type == 'head_inline_css'){
            addStyle(xmlhttp.responseText);
            }
        }
    }
    xmlhttp.open("GET", theUrl, true );
    xmlhttp.send();    
}

    <section class="section blog-contents"> 
      <div class="pa blog-editor">
        <div class="l-container">
          <div class="be__wrapper">
            <div class="be__contents">
              <div class="be__contents-wrapper">
                <h2><a id="post-136451-_4lt92rr5muov"></a>Executive Summary</h2>
<p>Our researchers discovered dozens of scam campaigns using deepfake videos featuring the likeness of various public figures, including CEOs, news anchors and top government officials. These campaigns appear in English, Spanish, French, Italian, Turkish, Czech and Russian. Each campaign typically targets potential victims in a single country, including Canada, Mexico, France, Italy, Turkey, Czechia, Singapore, Kazakhstan and Uzbekistan.</p>
<p>Due to their infrastructural and tactical similarities, we believe that many of these campaigns likely stem from a single threat actor group. We have observed this threat actor group using deepfake videos to spread fake investment schemes and fake government-sponsored giveaways.</p>
<p>As of June 2024, we had discovered hundreds of domains being used to promote these campaigns. Each domain has been accessed an average of 114,000 times globally since going live, based on our passive DNS (pDNS) telemetry.</p>
<p>Starting with a campaign promoting an investment scheme called Quantum AI, we studied the infrastructure behind this campaign to track its spread over time. Through this infrastructure investigation, we discovered several additional deepfake campaigns leveraging completely different themes that the same threat actor group created and promoted. These additional scam campaigns used different languages and the likeness of different public figures, suggesting that each campaign is intended for a different target audience.</p>
<p>Despite the use of generative AI (GenAI) in these campaigns, traditional investigative techniques remain useful to identify the hosting infrastructure leveraged by these threat actors. As the malicious usage of deepfake technology increases among threat actors, so should defenders’ efforts to proactively detect and prevent these types of attacks.</p>
<p>Customers of Palo Alto Networks are better protected from these attacks via <a href="https://www.paloaltonetworks.com/network-security/advanced-url-filtering" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Advanced URL Filtering</a>, which will continue to detect and block websites that are used to propagate deepfake-based scam campaigns.</p>
<table style="width: 100%;">
<thead>
<tr>
<td style="width: 35%;"><b>Related Unit 42 Topics</b></td>
<td style="width: 100%;"><a href="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/tag/scams/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><b>Scams</b></a>, <strong><a href="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/tag/phishing/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Phishing</a></strong></td>
</tr>
</thead>
</table>
<h2><a id="post-136451-_8m6193ki0xvr"></a>Discovering Quantum AI Hosting Infrastructure</h2>
<p>To study the Quantum AI campaign, we decided to analyze the infrastructure behind the websites hosting these attacks. Starting with an initial seed set of detections from our deepfake video detection pipeline, we then looked for additional websites serving up known malicious videos. We observed several Quantum AI-related videos that adversaries were widely sharing via websites hosted on newly registered domains.</p>
<p>Upon further investigation, we identified that the videos themselves were primarily hosted on a single domain:</p>
<ul>
<li><span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Belmar-marketing[.]online</span></li>
</ul>
<p>Next, we searched for other web pages that served video files from this domain and also contained keywords like <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Quantum AI</span> in the HTML content.</p>
<p>Through this process, we were able to uncover dozens of other scam pages using these videos as a lure. We then used the content on these web pages as well as the pathnames of the video files to create signatures to expand our detections. (See the <a href="#post-136451-_v8176g40kstn">Indicators of Compromise</a> section for example URLs.)</p>
<p>In May 2024, we noticed that an increasing number of Quantum AI videos were being hosted on other domains as well, including the following:</p>
<ul>
<li><span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Ai-usmcollective[.]click</span></li>
<li><span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Fortunatenews[.]com</span></li>
<li><span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Fiirststreeeet[.]top</span></li>
</ul>
<p>We also discovered some sites built using website builders that were promoting the same Quantum AI scam. In these cases, the attackers re-hosted the video directly on the site via the website builder, not on one of the shared video-hosting domains mentioned above.</p>
<h3><a id="post-136451-_ym7sbo70a2oe"></a>Quantum AI Example Videos and Web Pages</h3>
<p>In Figures 1-7, we present examples of Quantum AI scam web pages and videos discovered by our video analysis pipeline and infrastructure-based investigation. In most of these examples, the scam web page was hosted on a newly registered domain, and the video was hosted as an <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">.mp4</span> file on one of the shared video-hosting domains mentioned above (e.g., <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">belmar-marketing[.]online</span>).</p>
<p>In most cases, the attackers appear to have started with a legitimate video and added on their own AI-generated audio. Finally, they used lip-syncing technology to modify the lip movement of the speaker to match the AI-generated audio. Most of the videos use Elon Musk as their celebrity of choice, although we discovered a handful of examples using other public figures as well:</p>
<ul>
<li>Tucker Carlson</li>
<li>Lee Hsien Loong, the former Prime Minister of Singapore</li>
<li>Tharman Shanmugaratnam, the President of Singapore (as of June 2024)</li>
</ul>

<figure id="attachment_136464" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-136464" style="width: 1354px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img decoding="async" class="wp-image-136464 size-large" src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-477113-136451-7-1354x700.png" alt="A person in business attire is seated at a news desk with the words &quot;Quantum AI&quot; displayed below. The background features a plain, light-colored wall." width="1354" height="700" srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-477113-136451-7-1354x700.png 1354w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-477113-136451-7-786x406.png 786w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-477113-136451-7-768x397.png 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-477113-136451-7-1536x794.png 1536w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-477113-136451-7.png 2048w" sizes="(max-width: 1354px) 100vw, 1354px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-136464" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 7. A screenshot of a deepfake video of Tharman Shanmugaratnam, the current President of Singapore, used to promote the Quantum AI scam.</figcaption></figure>
<h2><a id="post-136451-_2an8ryq91inv"></a>Deepfake Campaign Discovery and Tracking</h2>
<p>After investigating the Quantum AI scam campaign, we explored broader trends surrounding these deepfake campaigns as a whole.</p>
<h3><a id="post-136451-_o29zwr42u3pj"></a>Uncovering Additional Deepfake Scams</h3>
<p>In addition to the Quantum AI scam, we also investigated the other videos that were present on these video-hosting domains. In doing so, we were able to uncover several other scam campaigns (likely propagated by the same threat actor group), many of which use deepfake videos as a lure. These deepfake videos typically use the likeness of public figures like CEOs, news anchors or top government officials.</p>
<p>We discovered deepfake videos in several different languages, including English, Spanish, French, Italian, Turkish, Czech and Russian. Each campaign typically targets potential victims in a single country, including Canada, Mexico, France, Italy, Turkey, Czechia, Singapore, Kazakhstan and Uzbekistan.</p>
<p>Similar to the Quantum AI scam campaign, these videos add AI-generated audio on top of an existing video and use lip-syncing tools to alter the lip movement of the speaker to match the new audio. Visitors to these web pages are prompted to register with their name and phone number, and they are instructed to await a call from an account manager or representative.</p>
<p>In many of these cases, we discovered several newly registered domains hosting the same content (and the same deepfake video lure). This means that each of these scam web pages is part of a larger campaign, not just a one-off scam web page.</p>
<p>For example, in the case of the KazMunayGas scam shown below in Figure 8, we found scammers using the same video across several recently registered domains, including:</p>
<ul>
<li><span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Aigroundwork[.]top</span></li>
<li><span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Aitfinside[.]shop</span></li>
<li><span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Block4aischeme[.]top</span></li>
<li><span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Systemaigroundwork[.]shop</span></li>
</ul>
<p>The <a href="#post-136451-_v8176g40kstn">Indicators of Compromise</a> section provides a more complete list of these domains.</p>
<p><figure id="attachment_136466" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-136466" style="width: 1169px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img decoding="async" class="wp-image-136466 size-large" src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-483208-136451-8-1169x700.png" alt="A news anchor reporting on a financial surge in Kazakhstani banks due to payments from KazMunayGas, displayed on a computer screen with multiple open browser tabs." width="1169" height="700" srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-483208-136451-8-1169x700.png 1169w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-483208-136451-8-735x440.png 735w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-483208-136451-8-768x460.png 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-483208-136451-8-1536x920.png 1536w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-483208-136451-8.png 2048w" sizes="(max-width: 1169px) 100vw, 1169px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-136466" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 8. <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Coinframework[.]top</span>, a scam website using an AI-manipulated video of a Kazakh news anchor to promote a fake giveaway started by KazMunayGas, the state-owned oil and gas company of Kazakhstan.</figcaption></figure><figure id="attachment_136468" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-136468" style="width: 1181px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img decoding="async" class="wp-image-136468 size-large" src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-488599-136451-9-1181x700.png" alt="Screenshot of the Kyivstar registration form webpage, featuring fields for name and phone number and an 'Apply now' button. Below is a comment section with a user testimonial about a quick money transfer." width="1181" height="700" srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-488599-136451-9-1181x700.png 1181w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-488599-136451-9-742x440.png 742w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-488599-136451-9-768x455.png 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-488599-136451-9-1536x911.png 1536w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-488599-136451-9.png 2048w" sizes="(max-width: 1181px) 100vw, 1181px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-136468" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 9. <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Riseanalyze[.]click</span>, a website linked to from <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">coinframework[.]top</span>. This website contains a registration form for the KazMunayGas-themed scam.</figcaption></figure>Although the languages and impersonation-targets of these scam campaigns are different, they share the following similarities:</p>
<ul>
<li>They all use similar deepfake techniques</li>
<li>They have similar calls to action</li>
<li>They host their videos on a small, shared set of domains (that do not seem to be used for any other purpose than to host these scam videos)</li>
</ul>
<p>This suggests that these campaigns can most likely be attributed to a single threat actor group.</p>
<p>We present some selected examples of these additional scam campaigns in Figures 10-15.</p>

<h3><a id="post-136451-_gj7oiqv0omoa"></a>Campaign Activity Over Time</h3>
<p>While these campaigns started about a year ago, we observed a large spike of newly observed domains (shown in Figure 16) in February 2024. Unlike typical phishing or malware domains, these domains are relatively long-lived, with an average active time of 142 days.</p>
<figure id="attachment_136480" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-136480" style="width: 712px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img decoding="async" class="wp-image-136480 size-medium" src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/chart-8-712x440.png" alt="Line graph showing the 'Number of Domains', over the months from July 2023 to May 2024. The graph shows fluctuations in domain numbers, peaking notably in February 2024." width="712" height="440" srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/chart-8-712x440.png 712w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/chart-8-1132x700.png 1132w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/chart-8-768x475.png 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/chart-8-1536x950.png 1536w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/chart-8.png 2048w" sizes="(max-width: 712px) 100vw, 712px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-136480" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 16. The number of newly observed domains hosting deepfake videos over time.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Figure 17 shows that the number of active domains exponentially increased until about March 2024, and the total number of active domains has remained steady to the present day.</p>
<figure id="attachment_136482" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-136482" style="width: 712px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img decoding="async" class="wp-image-136482 size-medium" src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/chart-9-712x440.png" alt="Line graph displaying the monthly growth in the number of domains from July 2023 to June 2024, with significant increases starting in January 2024. The graph starts at 7 domains and peaks at 175 domains by June 2024." width="712" height="440" srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/chart-9-712x440.png 712w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/chart-9-1132x700.png 1132w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/chart-9-768x475.png 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/chart-9-1536x950.png 1536w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/chart-9.png 2048w" sizes="(max-width: 712px) 100vw, 712px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-136482" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 17. The number of active domains hosting deepfake videos over time.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Furthermore, it is concerning to note that these domains have a high reach, with each domain being accessed an average of 114,000 times since they first went live, based on pDNS telemetry. The actual number is likely much higher.</p>
<h4><a id="post-136451-_wjqhpvsk6luh"></a>Hosting Infrastructure Analysis</h4>
<p>Going with the current trend of camouflaging in shared hosting infrastructure, 86.7% of these campaign domains are using the same popular content delivery network (CDN). Multiple IP addresses from the CDN host the same content across different geographic locations, with the U.S., the Netherlands and Russia being the top 3 locations. The utilization of CDNs makes it difficult to attribute the campaign to a particular threat actor or geolocation.</p>
<p>We observed that the attackers primarily hosted their videos on a small set of attacker-owned domains. Attackers presumably did this to circumvent takedown issues that could occur on more popular video-hosting platforms.</p>
<p>Until April 2024, we observed that the deepfake videos were predominantly hosted on <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">belmar-marketing[.]online</span>. However, starting in May 2024, the attackers began to rotate their video hosting locations more frequently. As such, we observed that videos were now mainly hosted on <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">fiirststreeeet[.]top</span>, <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">ai-usmcollective[.]click</span> and <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">fortunatenews[.]com</span>.</p>
<p>Looking for web pages that link to videos hosted on these domains has been very valuable for tracking the spread of these campaigns so far. We will continue to monitor for new video-hosting domains as these campaigns progress.</p>
<h2><a id="post-136451-_fv3bfmcufjdr"></a>How the Quantum AI Scam Works</h2>
<p>During our research, we observed posts and ads promoting Quantum AI on various social media platforms (shown in Figures 18-20). According to the Australian <a href="https://www.scamwatch.gov.au/news-alerts/scam-alert-fake-celebrity-online-investment-scams" target="_blank" rel="noopener">National Anti-Scam Center</a>, scammers often first use these sorts of social media ads or fake news articles to link to scam web pages that ask for the victim user’s contact information.</p>
<figure id="attachment_136484" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-136484" style="width: 580px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img decoding="async" class="wp-image-136484 size-medium" src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-537194-136451-18-580x440.png" alt="Tweet pinned by Quantum Trading Post X account. Elon Musk has thrown his support behind the Quantum AI revolution, signaling a future where we all stand to profit. This cutting-edge tech promises to redefine trading. 100% guaranteed profits. Video of Elon Musk speaking. Quantum AI logo. " width="580" height="440" srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-537194-136451-18-580x440.png 580w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-537194-136451-18-922x700.png 922w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-537194-136451-18-768x583.png 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-537194-136451-18.png 1242w" sizes="(max-width: 580px) 100vw, 580px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-136484" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 18. Social media post linking to a Quantum AI scam web page.</figcaption></figure>
<figure id="attachment_136486" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-136486" style="width: 487px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img decoding="async" class="wp-image-136486 size-large" src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-540791-136451-19-487x700.png" alt="Screenshot of a social media post from 'ELON_MUSK_BOT3' with a patterned green background and text promoting an investment opportunity. The post invites members to contact the admin for setting up an investment plan, highlighting acceptance of various cryptocurrencies like Bitcoin, Ethereum and more." width="487" height="700" srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-540791-136451-19-487x700.png 487w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-540791-136451-19-306x440.png 306w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-540791-136451-19-768x1104.png 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-540791-136451-19-1068x1536.png 1068w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-540791-136451-19.png 1242w" sizes="(max-width: 487px) 100vw, 487px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-136486" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 19. Messaging platform post linking to a Quantum AI scam web page.</figcaption></figure>
<figure id="attachment_136488" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-136488" style="width: 1920px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img decoding="async" class="wp-image-136488 size-large" src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-545582-136451-20-1920x672.png" alt="A person's hand holding a smartphone displaying an advertisement for joining QuantumAI. A laptop keyboard and bundles of 100 dollar bills are also visible on the desk. An accompanying Facebook post by &quot;Elon Musk Tesla Company&quot; encourages viewers to invest in Quantum AI." width="1920" height="672" srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-545582-136451-20-1920x672.png 1920w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-545582-136451-20-786x275.png 786w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-545582-136451-20-768x269.png 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-545582-136451-20-1536x538.png 1536w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-545582-136451-20.png 2048w" sizes="(max-width: 1920px) 100vw, 1920px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-136488" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 20. Social media post using a video to promote the Quantum AI scam.</figcaption></figure>
<p>After visiting the scam landing page and filling out a form to sign up for the platform, one of the scammers gives the victim a phone call. In this call, the scammer tells the victim they’ll need to pay around $250 to access the platform.</p>
<p>The scammer instructs the victim to download a special app so that they can “invest” more of their funds. Within the app, a dashboard appears to show small profits. From there, the scammers continue persuading the victim to deposit more of their money and may even allow the victim to withdraw a small amount of money as a way to gain trust.</p>
<p>Finally, when the victim tries to withdraw their funds, the scammers either demand withdrawal fees, or cite some other reason (e.g., tax issues) for not being able to get their funds back. The scammers may then lock the victim out of their account and pocket the remaining funds, causing the victim to have lost the majority of the money that they put into the “platform.”</p>
<h2><a id="post-136451-_wven14kmgum2"></a>Overview of the Web-Based Deepfake Scam Landscape</h2>
<p>Quantum AI is not the only scam that adversaries are using involving deepfakes. In this section we’ll discuss other techniques and services that they have been using.</p>
<p>In <a href="https://www.cnn.com/2024/02/04/asia/deepfake-cfo-scam-hong-kong-intl-hnk/index.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">early 2024</a>, a company lost $25 million to attackers who used deepfake technology to impersonate their chief financial officer on a video conferencing call. While video conferencing deepfakes have received significant attention as a result of this attack, web-based deepfake scams are an emerging threat that researchers should monitor as well.</p>
<p>2024 is predicted to be the largest voting year in history. Over <a href="https://www.vox.com/future-perfect/2024/1/3/24022864/elections-democracy-2024-united-states-india-pakistan-indonesia-european-parliament-far-right-voting" target="_blank" rel="noopener">60 countries</a> are holding significant elections this year, meaning that around half the world's population could be directly affected by these events. In response, <a href="https://www.politico.eu/article/deepfakes-distrust-disinformation-welcome-ai-election-2024/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">researchers have raised concerns</a> about the potential for deepfakes to promote political misinformation. However, the impact of deepfakes is not limited to the political domain. Cybercriminals have already been creating and sharing deepfake videos for their own malicious purposes.</p>
<h3><a id="post-136451-_atlgsxaki811"></a>Deepfakes Used to Promote Scams and Phishing Attacks</h3>
<p>Since the advent of GenAI, attackers have used deepfakes to promote political misinformation, and even to further voter outreach. For example, in early 2024, a Democratic political <a href="https://www.npr.org/2024/05/23/nx-s1-4977582/fcc-ai-deepfake-robocall-biden-new-hampshire-political-operative" target="_blank" rel="noopener">consultant used an audio deepfake</a> of <a href="https://apnews.com/article/new-hampshire-primary-biden-ai-deepfake-robocall-f3469ceb6dd613079092287994663db5" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Joe Biden</a> to discourage voters in the state of New Hampshire from voting in the upcoming primary election.</p>
<p>In India, <a href="https://www.wired.com/story/indian-elections-ai-deepfakes/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">politicians actively encouraged</a> their supporters to create deepfakes to promote their own candidacies. In 2022, an unknown <a href="https://www.npr.org/2022/03/16/1087062648/deepfake-video-zelenskyy-experts-war-manipulation-ukraine-russia" target="_blank" rel="noopener">threat actor used manipulated deepfake videos</a> of Ukrainian President Volodymir Zelensky as a part of information warfare in the Russia-Ukraine war.</p>
<p>Now, we are seeing cybercriminals start to use deepfake media to promote their own scams and phishing attacks as well. In recent months, reporters have observed scams impersonating figures like <a href="https://finance.yahoo.com/news/elon-musk-deepfake-crypto-scam-093000545.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Elon Musk</a> (shown in Figure 21), <a href="https://prestmit.io/blog/bill-gates-giving-away-bitcoin-unravelling-truth" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Bill Gates</a> and <a href="https://www.mediamatters.org/tiktok/deepfake-warren-buffett-selling-bitcoin-scams-tiktok-users" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Warren Buffett</a> to peddle fake cryptocurrencies, giveaways and other investment schemes. These are created with the ultimate goal of stealing funds from victims. (Our <a href="https://x.com/Unit42_Intel/status/1806725335595016531" target="_blank" rel="noopener">previous</a> <a href="https://twitter.com/Unit42_Intel/status/1793397014090178955" target="_blank" rel="noopener">tweets</a> on this topic have more details.)</p>
<p><figure id="attachment_136490" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-136490" style="width: 918px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img decoding="async" class="wp-image-136490 size-full" src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-550297-136451-21.png" alt="Elon Musk is featured in an NBC broadcast discussing Liberty Coins, with an inset image of a golden coin." width="918" height="737" srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-550297-136451-21.png 918w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-550297-136451-21-548x440.png 548w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-550297-136451-21-872x700.png 872w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-550297-136451-21-768x617.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 918px) 100vw, 918px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-136490" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 21. Screenshot of an Elon Musk deepfake video seen on <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">patriotsmaga2024[.]com</span>, a website promoting the sale of fake “Trump <a href="https://www.reuters.com/fact-check/no-evidence-trump-releasing-liberty-coins-alongside-bank-america-2024-04-22/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Liberty Coins</a>.”</figcaption></figure>Previously, these attackers might have used paid actors to promote their scams (e.g., by creating videos purporting to be a client who profited from a fake investment scheme). With the increasing popularity and effectiveness of tools that use AI to generate content (e.g., images, audio and video), attackers are now able to create these videos in a cheaper and more convincing way.</p>
<h3><a id="post-136451-_9r2buirwo9h2"></a>Deepfakes as a Service</h3>
<p>Our researchers have encountered cybercriminals selling, discussing and trading deepfake tooling and creation services across forums, social media chat channels and instant messaging platforms. These tools and services offer capabilities for generating deceptive and malicious content including audio, video and imagery. The ecosystem surrounding deepfake creation and tooling is alive and vibrant, and cybercriminals are selling a variety of options from face swapping tools to deepfake videos.</p>
<p>Face swapping tools like <a href="https://www.paloaltonetworks.com/blog/prisma-cloud/three-threats-generative-ai/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Swapface</a> (shown in Figure 22) range in price from free to over $249 a month. Adversaries abuse these tools, placing the videos they create on diverse platforms and social media platforms. Swapface offers user-friendly filters and face swapping that operates in real time, allowing users to alter or replace faces in videos.</p>
<figure id="attachment_136492" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-136492" style="width: 786px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img decoding="async" class="wp-image-136492 size-medium" src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-555521-136451-22-786x361.png" alt="Screenshot of SWAPFACE's pricing page showing various subscription plans ranging from a free tier to an Enterprise plan, detailing features like image faces per day, team access, and no tracker storage for each level." width="786" height="361" srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-555521-136451-22-786x361.png 786w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-555521-136451-22-1524x700.png 1524w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-555521-136451-22-768x353.png 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-555521-136451-22-1536x705.png 1536w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-555521-136451-22.png 1740w" sizes="(max-width: 786px) 100vw, 786px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-136492" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 22. Swapface tooling subscription cost.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The criminal application of deepfake tooling and creation services and tools includes the following activities:</p>
<ul>
<li>Facilitating the creation of fake identities</li>
<li>Committing bank fraud</li>
<li>Orchestrating disinformation campaigns</li>
<li>Bypassing know-your-customer verification checks</li>
<li>Performing cryptocurrency theft</li>
</ul>
<p>These services can manipulate visuals and audio with alarming precision, leading to significant ethical and security concerns. The cost of generating a deepfake video can vary widely, typically ranging from $60 to $500, reflecting the complexity and quality of the requested forgery.</p>
<p>As seen in Figure 23, we also discovered messaging platform channels specifically advertising the creation of deepfake videos for scam purposes.</p>
<figure id="attachment_136494" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-136494" style="width: 1297px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img decoding="async" class="wp-image-136494 size-large" src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-560692-136451-23-1297x700.png" alt="Channel by Deepfakes from SM Crew. Posts show two seperate videos. Channel profile shows 37 subscribers, an anime character and A$AP Rocky, information in Cyrillic and some redacted text. " width="1297" height="700" srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-560692-136451-23-1297x700.png 1297w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-560692-136451-23-786x424.png 786w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-560692-136451-23-768x414.png 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/word-image-560692-136451-23.png 1364w" sizes="(max-width: 1297px) 100vw, 1297px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-136494" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 23. Messaging platform channel dedicated to deepfake generation services.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The accessibility and range of costs make deepfakes particularly versatile tools for maliciousness, posing challenges for both individuals and institutions trying to safeguard against fraud and misinformation.</p>
<h2><a id="post-136451-_vsllukdzec96"></a>Conclusion</h2>
<p>Despite the use of GenAI in these campaigns, traditional investigative techniques remain useful to identify the hosting infrastructure leveraged by these threat actors. As threat actors increase their use of deepfake technology, organizations should also proactively defend against these types of attacks.</p>
<p>Palo Alto Networks researchers will continue to monitor these deepfake-based scam campaigns and continue to discover and investigate additional deepfake-based scam campaigns. As such, we can ensure that our customers are better protected from them via <a href="https://www.paloaltonetworks.com/network-security/advanced-url-filtering" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Advanced URL Filtering</a>.</p>
<h2><a id="post-136451-_v8176g40kstn"></a>Indicators of Compromise</h2>

                <div class="g-recaptcha" data-expired-callback="captchaExpires" data-callback="captchaComplete" data-sitekey="6Lc5EhgTAAAAAJa-DzE7EeWABasWg4LKv-R3ao6o"></div>

<script>

(function($) {
	// Migrated from the unit42-v5 + Modifications
	var subscribeSuccess = false;
	var email = document.getElementById('newsletter-email');
	var subscription_form = document.getElementById('unit42footerSubscription_form');
	var subscription_form_button = document.getElementById('unit42footerSubscription_form_button');
	window.captchaComplete = function() {
		subscribeSuccess = true;
		if ($(mail).val() != '' && isEmail($(mail).val())) {
			$(subscription_form_button).removeClass('is-disabled');
		}
		setTimeout(function() {
			$(email).focus();
			$('.g-recaptcha iframe').attr('tabindex', '-1');
		}, 100)
	}
	window.captchaExpires = function() {
		subscribeSuccess = false;
		$(subscription_form_button).addClass('is-disabled', true);
	} 
	$(subscription_form).submit(function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		e.stopImmediatePropagation();
		updateEmailMask();
		var success = true;
		var form = $(this);
		var mail = form.find('input[name="Email"]');
		
		if (mail.val() === '') {
			mail.addClass('has-error');
			showError(1);
			success = false;	
		}  else if (!isEmail(mail.val())){
			showError(2);
			success = false;
		}
		else {
			mail.removeClass('has-error');
			$('.error-mail').addClass('d-none');
		}

		if (!subscribeSuccess) {
			$('.error-recaptcha').removeClass('d-none');
		} else {
			$('.error-recaptcha').addClass('d-none');
		}

		if (success && subscribeSuccess) {
			$.ajax({
				type: 'POST',
				url: form.attr('action'),
				data: form.serialize(),
				beforeSend: function() {
                 form.find('button').addClass('is-loading');
    			},
				success: function(msg) {
					form.find('.form-success-message').html('<p class="success-message">You have been successfully subscribed</p>');
					form.find('button').removeClass('is-loading');
					$(email).val('');
					clearError();
				},
				error: function(jqXHR, textStatus, errorThrown) {
					$(subscription_form_button).addClass('is-disabled', true);
					form.find('button').removeClass('is-loading');
					
				}
			});
		}
		return false;
	});
	function showError(error_type){
		if(error_type == 1) {
			$('.error-mail').text("Please enter the email address.").addClass('error-show');
			$(subscription_form_button).addClass('is-disabled');
		} else if(error_type == 2){
			$('.error-mail').text("Please provide a valid e-mail address.").addClass('error-show');
			$(subscription_form_button).addClass('is-disabled');
		}	
		$(subscription_form_button).removeClass('is-loading');
	}
	function clearError(){
		$('.error-mail').text("").removeClass('error-show');;
		$(subscription_form_button).removeClass('is-loading');
		$(subscription_form_button).removeClass('is-disabled');
	}
	
	$(email).on('input', function (event) { 
		var email = $(this).val();
		if (isEmail(email) ) {			
			clearError();
		} else if(email == ""){
			clearError();
		} else{
			showError(2);			  
		}
    });

	function isEmail(email) {
		var re = /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
		return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
	}
	
	var captcha_loaded = false;
         if(!captcha_loaded){
            // recaptcha on foucs call
            $(document).on('change paste keyup', '#newsletter-email', function () {
               if($('.g-recaptcha').hasClass('d-none')){
                $('.g-recaptcha').removeClass('d-none');
               }
               if(!captcha_loaded ){
                  captcha_loaded  = true;
                  // trigger loading api.js (recaptcha.js) script
                  var head = document.getElementsByTagName('head')[0];
                  var script = document.createElement('script');
                  script.type = 'text/javascript';
                  script.src = 'https://www.google.com/recaptcha/api.js?hl=en_US';
                  head.appendChild(script);
               }
            });
        }
	
	function updateEmailMask() {
		var email = $("#unit42footerSubscription_form input[name='Email']").val();
		if (email && email.trim() != '') {
			var maskedEmail = maskEmailAddress(email);
			$("#unit42footerSubscription_form input[name='emailFormMask']").val(maskedEmail);
		}
	}

	function maskEmailAddress (emailAddress) {
		function mask(str) {
			var strLen = str.length;
			if (strLen > 4) {
				return str.substr(0, 1) + str.substr(1, strLen - 1).replace(/\w/g, '*') + str.substr(-1,1);
			}
			return str.replace(/\w/g, '*');
		}
		return emailAddress.replace(/([\w.]+)@([\w.]+)(\.[\w.]+)/g, function (m, p1, p2, p3) {
			return mask(p1) + '@' + mask(p2) + p3;
		});

		return emailAddress;
	}

}(jQuery));
//# sourceMappingURL=main.js.map
	
</script>
<!--  End: Footer subscription form -->

    <script type="text/javascript">
	var isProcessing = false; 
    function alter_ul_post_values(obj,post_id,ul_type){
	
		if (isProcessing)    
		return;  
		isProcessing = true;   
		var like_nonce = jQuery('#_wpnonce').val();
		jQuery(obj).find("span").html("..");
                jQuery.ajax({
                    type: "POST",
                    url: "https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/plugins/like-dislike-counter-for-posts-pages-and-comments/ajax_counter.php",
                    data: "post_id="+post_id+"&up_type="+ul_type+"&ul_nonce="+like_nonce,
                    success: function(msg){
                            jQuery(obj).find("span").html(msg);
                            isProcessing = false; 
                            jQuery(obj).find('svg').children('path').attr('stroke','#0050FF');
                            jQuery(obj).removeClass('idc_ul_cont_not_liked idc_ul_cont_not_liked_inner');
                    }
 		});
	}
	</script>

function loadScript(url, defer){
    var script1 = document.createElement('script');
    script1.setAttribute('type', 'text/javascript');
    script1.setAttribute('src',url);
    if(defer == true){
        script1.setAttribute('defer','defer');
    }
    document.head.appendChild(script1);
}
function loadScript1(url, callback){

    var script = document.createElement("script")
    script.type = "text/javascript";
    if (script.readyState){  //IE
        script.onreadystatechange = function(){
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" || script.readyState == "complete"){
                script.onreadystatechange = null;
                callback();
            }
        };
    } else {  //Others
        script.onload = function(){
            callback();
        };
    }
    script.src = url;
    document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
}
